"You almost breached the edge," she said low, voice threading the quiet like a vector drawn careful. "The lines frayed to nothing at the node. I couldn't map it fast enough—"
He crossed the space between them deliberate, tremor-hands framing her face gentle as testing a fragile weld fresh from the pour. "You held me true regardless. That's enough—more than." The warmth stirred unbidden, copper threading to her blue not for metal or mend, but something softer. He leaned in, lips brushing hers tentative at first, then sure as a pin seating—a mend of edges long braced apart, his pull yielding to her form in the contact.
She answered the kiss, her stiff fingers threading through his hair with measured care, the hold a shared load: precision softening into connection, vulnerability bleeding through the press like warmth rerouting a warp. Barriers cracked in controlled measure—not shattered wild, but yielded deliberate, fears voiced silent in the grip.
They drew back slow, breaths mingling in the forge's warmth. The room held steady, world unpunished for the deviation. "This," she said, the corners of her mouth turning honest in a small, true arc. "We keep it."
"Keep it," he agreed, palm pressing to her cheek, the vein-line steadying under the touch, her tremor easing a fraction in the shared circuit. Barriers down but not discarded—clamped now, braced mutual. The forge warmed unbidden around them, coals blooming faint as if resonance answered the mend. Rhythm remade, softer at the edges.
Chapter 13: Morning-Of — (Jhace POV)
The anneal dawned with tools laid in neat row on the workbench, the city feigning a level reason under the kindling wash seeping through vents, but Jhace didn't trust the pretense—plans built like braces, meant to shift load where damage landed least. He unrolled the chalk map across the scarred wood, Tiffani's overnight vectors tracing load paths for the market span, braced against the cant's unrelenting pull. Twelve tides since the cut, rumors walked the streets in paper shoes: pamphlets muttering "endings west" in woodcut letters that thought themselves brave but cracked under scrutiny.
"Sequence," he said over the map, finger tracing the central cross-line. "Site A primary, shift to B only if the world's moods permit—no forcing the torque."
"Pre-shape the node here," Tiffani added, her tap light on the marked junction. "It buys us the turn, bleeds the east deviation before it stacks."
"Logged," Chloen said from her stool, her script flowing confident now—competence earned tide by tide, no longer the nervous tally but a quick-study with marks that held scribe-true.
They ran the morning like a clean machine pour: Jhace pointed flaws without taking the wheel, his tremor baseline at fifty percent no longer fit for heavy torque; Bram pulled the loads steady and uncomplaining; Tiffani held smart rather than straining her eighty mobility, her sight scribing vectors that preempted failures; Chloen commanded a vendor off a suspect hanger with a stare sharp as a bracer's edge, no words needed.
Eyes watched from the edges—crowd gathering like weather, heat pressing on skin without direct glare. Bram handed over a copper bracer he'd cut down and refit, the metal scuffed but solid. "Wear this," he said, buckling it onto Jhace's wrist himself. "Doesn't make you immortal. Just makes you honest about the costs."
Jhace flexed under the weight, feeling it dual-edged: protection granted, but a reminder someone saw his need. "No need to father me," he said, no cruelty in the push-back.
"I'm not," Bram replied even. "I'm crewing you."
Jhace nodded once, the bracer settling like a new baseline. They climbed the flight to the last rib, Tiffani's step faltering half a count—not from weakness, but foresight's heavy load pulling her a breath ahead. He offered his palm up between them, tool-like, no boyish reach.
She placed her hand there, pace matching seamless. "One person," Chloen teased light from behind, and they let it stand uncorrected—truth in the shorthand. The rib reached as a unit, the day poised to try its take. It would fail against the brace.
Chapter 14: Weight Test — (Tiffani POV)
The site waited with its patient wrongness: hangers leaning a hair off plumb, the wall's posture slouched from over-loved use, deviations stacking where crowds had pressed too heavy in the tides since the cut. Tiffani placed her palms to the central cross, geometry sight mapping the surface tension deep into structure—flow dictating shape, load paths fraying at nodes she'd predicted. She could hold this if paid correctly, tolerances braced against the cant.
"Clamp," Jhace echoed her unspoken call, the word a partnership rather than mere repetition, his tremor hands steady at fifty baseline.
They bled the first head deliberate, hum dropping measured; the crowd—thinned from yesterday's theater—settled into watching without demand for spectacle, a weather of eyes but no storm yet.
Halfway through the sequence, the far-left hanger sang sharp and off-key. Jhace moved instinct—then halted, the new courage learned in their shared costs. He pointed instead; Bram took the wheel without word. Tiffani deepened her hold at the cross, fine control fraying at the edges like a string pulled too long under load.
"Stop," Jhace said, and she wanted to argue—the channel held, vectors still true—but the pact demanded obedience both ways, no deviation. She stepped off the hold, fingers shaking in the small, controlled way that signaled spent true, costs logged without waste.
They reset the sequence deliberate, finished the bleed. The wall forgave them their human measure, settling true under the adjusted load.
The declaration arrived as structural necessity—she could not carry the next span without voicing the load path that aligned it all. "I need your hand," she said to Jhace, taking it without waiting for approval, the grip earned a dozen times this anneal alone.
The crowd made its little sound, a murmur like pressure building. She ignored it, eyes on him. "I love you," she said, the words arranging the rest of her into true—not performance, but a load path clear and functional.
He didn't echo; he braced it. "We'll hold," he said, the promise shaping like a ring on a hanger: not pretty, absolutely necessary.
Chloen's face went soft in the way of finding home in a sentence uninvited; Bram's mouth twitched and held, a man allowing his private graces space.
They finished the site with hands at fifty percent reliable and trust absolute, the wall singing steady under test. The city didn't clap—no need, the hold was its own proof.
Chapter 15: Set True — (Jhace POV)
Afternoon put a hard, unflinching light on Rib Three, every flaw confessing like chalk hashes gone feral under the glare. The public phases had been promised by men in boots who carried no tools, no chalk, no keys—demands for spectacle where work needed quiet measure. They would do it anyway, sequence by sequence.
"Sequence," Jhace said, the word cutting the air less stupid, more braced.
They began: Tiffani held at the cross with control that had cost her the full day, her hands at sixty percent now, blue-silver clear; Bram took the wheels with the patience of a floodplain bearing load; Chloen made gauge numbers into commands, her multi-resonance budding like a vein-trace under skin.
The first phase stood solid. The second wavered, thought hard about failure, then remembered its manners under their shared pull.
On the third, the east-face hanger pin decided honesty about its limits—it went with a clean bang, the wheel lurching wild. Jhace didn't think; he moved—left hand to wheel, right to pry, body slotting between metal and the people below. Tremor turned his grip into a bad instrument; he compensated with stance, weight hung full.
The wheel tried to break his wrist in the torque. Bram's arm appeared under his like a brace unbudgeted but grateful-found, taking half the load. Tiffani's voice cut under the noise: "Release." He did, survival learned in their pact.
The wheel spun free; the hanger seated ugly at first, then true as the load redistributed. The wall groaned deep but decided to keep being a wall, hum settling ragged but intact.
Jhace staggered two steps back, the ground tilting his way now, not the world's. He went to a knee he didn't entirely trust, vein pulling deeper like something written permanent—heat licking up his forearm, not burn or itch but wire drawn tight under skin.
"Numbers," he rasped through a mouth that didn't want the work.
"Three heads," Chloen said, voice steady. "Stable. Holding stable."
He got to his feet slow, pride a tool he used when it served the job. "Again."
They set the last phase deliberate, the crowd breathing around them like a reminder that breath wasn't guaranteed. After, on the roof—truths' place since the first person looked down and decided to try again—they stood in the wind, letting bones cool from the pour.
Tiffani lifted her palm up; he set his to it, mirror to their first pull. He kissed her mouth. Then her palm—a vow etched deeper.
"You're at 3.0," she said, not accusation but record.
"Permanent," he replied, not bravado but fact.
"We plan around it," she said. "Costs don't make us holy. They make us careful."
"Careful keeps people alive," Bram put in from the roof's edge, pretending not to listen by staring at the horizon like men do with sunsets.
The city below had learned some weight, forgotten some vanity—posters at corner ribs muttering "lines snap north," wind making noise like a brace deciding to stay.
They sat backs to the proof-rib. Chloen wrapped her burned hand with new gauze, self-taught and steady.
"Next," Jhace said once breath agreed useful.
"Scale work," Tiffani said. "Private holds. Crew training. No performances. Publish a field sheet that says no in three polite ways and one impolite."
"Make the impolite one large," Bram grunted.
"Costs logged," Chloen said, writing. "Vein three point zero. Permanent. Hands at fifty. Tremor baseline." She looked up, dared the brace. "And four people who don't work alone anymore."
Jhace let it sit—no itch, just a pin seated under load admitted true.
He looked at Tiffani's palm, kissed it smaller. "What now," he said, and for the first time in a long time, the answer wasn't alone.
END

==== MEASUREMENT-LEXICON-COMPLETE.md ====
# CONFLUENCE CHRONICLES: COMPLETE MEASUREMENT LEXICON
## EXPONENTIAL SYSTEMS FOR TIME, DISTANCE, WEIGHT, VOLUME, PRESSURE & MORE
### Production-Ready Reference for N01-N30

---

## DOCUMENT PURPOSE

This lexicon provides **craft-based measurement systems** for Te'Oga that mirror real-world functionality while maintaining forge/glass cultural aesthetics. All measurements use **exponential scaling** (like the temporal system) to feel authentic and systematic.

**Status:** CANON — mandatory for all 30 novellas  
**Integration:** Matches Master Lexicon temporal system exactly

---

# SECTION 1: TEMPORAL SYSTEM (CANONICAL)

## Quick Reference

| Unit | Real-World Equivalent | Te'Oga Term | Usage |
|------|----------------------|-------------|-------|
| **Day** | 24 hours | **Tide** | "Within the tide" |
| **Week** | 5 days | **Anneal** | "Before the anneal cools" |
| **Month** | 35 days (7 anneals) | **Crucible** | "A crucible of mourning" |
| **Year** | 315 days (9 crucibles) | **Casting** | "Many castings ago" |
| **Decade** | 10 years | **Smelting** | "In my third smelting" |
| **Century** | 100 years | **Masterwork** | "Three Masterworks past" |
| **Millennium** | 1,000 years | **Epoch / Fusion** | "Since the Second Fusion" |
| **Eon** | Geological time | **The Crucible** | "As old as the Crucible" |

---

## Five Daily Periods (Within Each Tide)

1. **Kindling (Dawn)** — First Tide; work begins
2. **Pouring (Mid-morning)** — Second Tide; full energy
3. **Shaping (Noon)** — Third Tide; peak heat/output
4. **Striking (Afternoon)** — Fourth Tide; refinement
5. **The Quench (Dusk)** — Fifth Tide; cooling/rest

---

## Five Days of the Anneal (Week)

1. **Heattide** — Preparation, gathering
2. **Pourtide** — Beginning work, activation
3. **Shapetide** — Formation, peak effort
4. **Striketide** — Refinement, precision
5. **Cooltide** — Settling, completion

---

## Seven Anneals of the Crucible (Month)

1. **First Heat** — Foundation, planning
2. **Rising Glow** — Momentum, active work
3. **Full Blaze** — Peak intensity, crisis
4. **Steady Burn** — Recovery, stabilization
5. **Ember Anneal** — Consolidation, maintained heat
6. **Fading Coals** — Waning, transition
7. **Final Temper** — Resolution, hardening

---

## Nine Crucibles of the Casting (Year)

### First Forge (Early Season — Crucibles 1-3)
1. **Crucible of Iron Roots** — Foundation
2. **Crucible of Rising Frames** — Structure
3. **Crucible of Skeletal Form** — Completion

### The Great Blow (Middle Season — Crucibles 4-6)
4. **Crucible of Molten Sand** — Chaos
5. **Crucible of Crystal Breath** — Transition
6. **Crucible of Prismatic Fire** — Transformation

### Fusion Season (Late Season — Crucibles 7-9)
7. **Crucible of Marriage** — Integration
8. **Crucible of Setting** — Refinement
9. **Crucible of Final Temper** — Hardening

---

## Mathematical Reference (Temporal)

| Unit | Tides | Anneals | Crucibles | Castings |
|------|-------|---------|-----------|----------|
| Tide | 1 | — | — | — |
| Anneal | 5 | 1 | — | — |
| Crucible | 35 | 7 | 1 | — |
| Casting | 315 | 63 | 9 | 1 |
| Smelting | 3,150 | 630 | 90 | 10 |
| Masterwork | 31,500 | 6,300 | 900 | 100 |
| Epoch | 315,000 | 63,000 | 9,000 | 1,000 |

# SECTION 2: DISTANCE / LENGTH SYSTEM

## Exponential Scale (Body-to-World)

| Unit | Approximate Real-World | Base Ratio | Usage |
|------|----------------------|------------|-------|
| **Finger** | ~2cm (digit width) | 1× | Smallest precision |
| **Hand** | ~10cm (palm width) | 5× finger | Small measurements |
| **Span** | ~23cm (hand spread) | 2.3× hand | Arm measurements |
| **Forearm** | ~45cm (elbow to fingertips) | 2× span | Body-scale work |
| **Stride** | ~90cm (walking step) | 2× forearm | Personal movement |
| **Bar** | ~1.8m (full arm reach) | 2× stride | Room/workshop scale |
| **Rod** | ~9m (forge hall width) | 5× bar | Building scale |
| **Cable** | ~45m (street block) | 5× rod | District scale |
| **Vein-span** | ~225m (heat-grid section) | 5× cable |

## DISTANCE

| Unit | Approx | Example |
|------|--------|---------|
| Finger | ~2cm | "Three fingers deep" |
| Hand | ~10cm | "A hand's clearance" |
| Span | ~23cm | "Two spans from bolt-seat" |
| Forearm | ~45cm | "Three forearms long" |
| Stride | ~90cm | "Five strides across" |
| **Bar** | **~1.8m** | **"Six bars nose to tail"** |
| **Rod** | **~9m** | **"Twelve rods before turning"** |
| Cable | ~45m | "Two cables east" |
| Vein-span | ~225m | "Three vein-spans of open ground" |
| Circuit | ~1.1km | "Half a circuit away" |
| Grid | ~5.5km | "Four grids total" |
| Reach | ~27.5km | "Two reaches to find him" |
| Expanse | ~137km | "Divided the expanse" |

**Quick:** 1 Bar = 4 Strides = 8 Forearms = 180 Fingers

|------|--------|---------|

| **Load** | **~375kg** | **"Full load of iron bar"** |
| Ingot | ~18,750kg | "Half an ingot of beam" |
| Pour | ~937 tonnes | "Full pour for riser" |

## VOLUME

| Unit | Approx | Example |
|------|--------|---------|

## TEMPERATURE (OBSERVATIONAL)

| Term | Visual | Use |
|------|--------|-----|
| Chill | Cold to touch | Ambient cold |
| Hand-warm | Body temp | Comfortable |
| Breath-steam | Condensation | Warming |
| **Blood heat** | **Dull red** | **Forging starts** |
| **Cherry** | **Bright red** | **Forging temp** |
| Orange | Orange glow | High forging |
| **Lemon** | **Yellow** | **Steel melting** |
| **White** | **White-hot** | **Glass working** |
| Blinding | Too bright | Danger |

**Example:** "Heat to cherry, hold five breaths, strike three sets."

# DISTANCE CONVERSIONS

## Metric → Te'Oga

| If You're Thinking... | Write Instead... | Ratio |
|----------------------|------------------|-------|
| 1-3 cm | fingers | 1 finger ≈ 2cm |
| 5-15 cm | hands | 1 hand ≈ 10cm |
| 20-30 cm | spans | 1 span ≈ 23cm |
| 40-50 cm | forearms | 1 forearm ≈ 45cm |
| 80-100 cm | strides | 1 stride ≈ 90cm |
| 1.5-2 m | bars | 1 bar ≈ 1.8m |
| 8-10 m | rods | 1 rod ≈ 9m |
| 40-50 m | cables | 1 cable ≈ 45m |
| 200-250 m | vein-spans | 1 vein-span ≈ 225m |
| 1 km | circuits | 1 circuit ≈ 1.1km |
| 5 km | grids | 1 grid ≈ 5.5km |
| 25 km | reaches | 1 reach ≈ 27.5km |
| 100-150 km | expanses | 1 expanse ≈ 137km |

---

## Imperial → Te'Oga

| If You're Thinking... | Write Instead... | Ratio |
|----------------------|------------------|-------|
| 1 inch | 1-2 fingers | 1 inch ≈ 1.3 fingers |
| 4 inches | 1 hand | 4 inches ≈ 10cm ≈ 1 hand |
| 9 inches | 1 span | 9 inches ≈ 23cm ≈ 1 span |
| 18 inches | 2 spans or 1 forearm | 18 inches ≈ 45cm |
| 1 yard | 1 bar | 1 yard ≈ 0.9m ≈ half a bar |
| 6 feet | 1 bar | 6 feet ≈ 1.8m ≈ 1 bar |
| 30 feet | 1 rod | 30 feet ≈ 9m ≈ 1 rod |
| 150 feet | 1 cable | 150 feet ≈ 45m ≈ 1 cable |
| 750 feet | 1 vein-span | 750 feet ≈ 225m ≈ 1 vein-span |
| 0.7 miles | 1 circuit | 0.7 miles ≈ 1.1km ≈ 1 circuit |
| 3.5 miles | 1 grid | 3.5 miles ≈ 5.5km ≈ 1 grid |
| 17 miles | 1 reach | 17 miles ≈ 27.5km ≈ 1 reach |
| 85 miles | 1 expanse | 85 miles ≈ 137km ≈ 1 expanse |

# SECTION 16: MATHEMATICAL QUICK REFERENCE

## Core Scaling Ratios

**Time System:** Alternating ×5 and ×7 scaling  
**Distance System:** Alternating ×2 and ×5 scaling  
**Weight System:** Consistent ×50 scaling  
**Volume System:** Consistent ×50 scaling  
**Pressure System:** ×5 and ×10 scaling  
**Speed System:** Doubling pattern  

---

## Conversion Cheat Sheet

### Distance
- 1 Bar = 4 Strides = 180 Fingers
- 1 Rod = 5 Bars = 900 Fingers
- 1 Circuit = 5 Vein-spans = ~1 km

### Weight
- 1 Stone = 50 Handfuls = 2,500 Pinches
- 1 Load = 50 Stone = 2,500 Handfuls
- 1 Ingot = 50 Loads = 2,500 Stone

### Volume
- 1 Jar = 50 Cups = 2,500 Thimbles
- 1 Cask = 50 Jars = 2,500 Cups
- 1 Vat = 50 Casks = 2,500 Jars

### Time (Sub-Tide)
- 1 Turn = 5 Watches = 25 Spells
- 1 Shift = 5 Turns = 125 Spells
- 1 Tide = 5 Shifts = 625 Spells

---

| Unit | Real-World Equivalent | Description | Usage |
|------|----------------------|-------------|-------|
| **Breath** | ~3 seconds (one cycle) | Single breath | Immediate timing |
| **Stroke** | ~6 seconds (hammer blow) | Tool operation | Work rhythm |

| **Spell** | ~2.5 minutes (5 sets) | Brief duration | Task completion |
| **Watch** | ~12.5 minutes (5 spells) | Attention span | Shift breaks |
| **Turn** | ~1 hour (5 watches) | Work period | Major task blocks |
| **Shift** | ~5 hours (5 turns) | Daily work period | One tide-period |

**What This Story Is Really About:**

Two people who speak through their handsâ€”one heals with warmth, one builds with precisionâ€”discover each other in the wreckage of a dying world. They don't just fall in love. Their partnership is the infrastructure that holds when everything else breaks.

This is **not** a story about magic saving the day. This is about two people learning that holding onâ€”to each other, to their work, to hopeâ€”costs everything and is still worth it.

It was the sound of Te’Oga waking, of a city drawing its first geothermal breath. First light was a lie down here. There was only the grid, and the work.\n\nChalk dust, fine as powdered bone, coated his hands. The air tasted of limestone, old iron, and the faint, clean scent of superheated steam. He followed Bram down the narrow access corridor, their footsteps echoing in the cathedral quiet. Bram, his mentor for a decade and the closest thing to a father he had left, moved with the easy economy of a man who had walked these same paths for thirty years. His gait was a language Jhace knew by heart.\n\n“Rising Glow, Casting 423,” Bram said, his voice a low rumble that the')

\# THE GRIP THAT HOLDS — 

\---

\#\# Chapter 1: Something Wrong — (Jhace POV)

Kindling light seeped down the Underface in a thin wash, barely enough to make the chalk marks shine. Jhace tasted limestone dust and old heat. The grid hummed under his boots—good tone, steady, a watch's worth since the last check. He ran his thumb along a riser seam anyway, feeling for the small betrayals: a grit line, a warmth that wasn't earned, a whisper where there should be a throat-sung note.

"Torque key," he said.

Chloen already had it out, two spans of oiled steel, teeth still sharp. She moved like a tally of nerves wrapped in a hand of resolve. Bram stood back with the posture of a man pretending to be at rest, copper bracer scuffed to the bone under its patina. He pretended a lot. Never about the work.

"Saddle pin's shy a quarter-turn," Jhace said. "Hear it?"

Chloen cocked her head. "I hear hum."

"Hum's not the song," Bram said. "What's the song, girl?"

Chloen squinted, tongue pinned against a molar as if that might wring sound from steel. The grid breathed through the riser—soft, regular, three heads of pressure on the gauge window, fogged at the edges. A good note rose in the forearm

print(lex[wt_start:vol_start])

print(lex[vol_start:temp_start])

[TOOL]
## Weight — DO NOT USE

| Forbidden | Use Instead |
|-----------|-------------|
| gram, g | grain, pinch |
| kilogram, kg | stone |
| pound, lb | stone |
| ton, tonne | ingot, pour |
| ounce, oz | handful |


----
## Volume — DO NOT USE

| Forbidden | Use Instead |
|-----------|-------------|
| milliliter, ml | drop, thimble |
| liter, L | cup, jar |
| gallon | cask |
| barrel | cask, vat |

[ASSISTANT]
time_start = lex.find("Time — DO NOT USE")
print(lex[time_start:time_start+400])

[TOOL]
Time — DO NOT USE

| Forbidden | Use Instead |
|-----------|-------------|
| second, sec | breath, stroke |
| minute, min | set, spell |
| hour, hr | watch, turn |
| day | tide |
| week | anneal |
| month | crucible |
| year | casting |

import re, textwrap, math

# Use the gthN01 content
text = gth_n01

# Create line index
lines = text.splitlines()
# Precompute cumulative char offset per line for future mapping if needed
offsets = []
total = 0
for line in lines:
    offsets.append(total)
    total += len(line)+1  # +1 for '\n'


# Build chapter mapping: line index -> chapter title
chapter_by_line = {}
current_chapter = "PREAMBLE"
for i, line in enumerate(lines):
    m = re.match(r"^##\s+(.+)", line.strip())
    if m:
        current_chapter = m.group(1)
    chapter_by_line[i] = current_chapter

# banned terms from lexicon
banned = {
    "distance": ["centimeter","cm","meter","kilometer","km","mile","inch","foot","yard"],
    "weight": ["gram","kilogram","kg","pound","lb","ton","tonne","ounce","oz"],
    "volume": ["milliliter","ml","liter","l","gallon","barrel"],
    "temperature": ["degrees","celsius","fahrenheit"],
    "time": ["second","sec","minute","min","hour","hr","day","week","month","year"],
}

# also banned forms singular/plural: we can let regex handle by matching base + optional 's', 'es'
# But some (lb, kg, cm) don't plural so simple.

# Build combined pattern with word boundaries, case-insensitive
# We'll treat 'l' as liter only if uppercase L or followed by 'iter'; but we don't want to flag random 'l'. So for volume we include 'liter' & 'liters', 'L' as stand-alone capital
banned_words = set()
for cat, words in banned.items():
    for w in words:
        banned_words.add(w.lower())

banned_words

[ASSISTANT]
import bisect

# Build alt pattern from banned_words
# We already excluded bare 'l'
terms = sorted(banned_words, key=len, reverse=True)
pattern = re.compile(r"\b(" + "|".join(re.escape(t) for t in terms) + r")s?\b", re.IGNORECASE)

matches = []
for m in pattern.finditer(text):
    term = m.group(0)
    pos = m.start()
    # find line index
    line_idx = bisect.bisect_right(offsets, pos) - 1
    chapter = chapter_by_line.get(line_idx, "UNKNOWN")
    # get context line
    line = lines[line_idx]
    matches.append((term, chapter, line_idx+1, line.strip()))

len(matches)

for term, chapter, line_no, line in matches:
    by_chapter[chapter].append((term, line_no, line))

for chapter, items in by_chapter.items():
    print("=== ", chapter, " ===")
    for term, line_no, line in items:
        print(f"{line_no:4d}: [{term}] {line}")
    print()

[ASSISTANT]
# rebuild chapter_by_line using "Chapter" occurrences
chapter_by_line = {}
current = "UNKNOWN"
for i, line in enumerate(lines):
    m = re.search(r"Chapter\s+\d+:[^\\\n]*", line)
    if m:
        current = m.group(0).strip()
    chapter_by_line[i] = current

# recompute matches with new mapping
matches = []
for m in pattern.finditer(text):
    term = m.group(0)
    pos = m.start()
    line_idx = bisect.bisect_right(offsets, pos) - 1
    chapter = chapter_by_line.get(line_idx, "UNKNOWN")
    line = lines[line_idx]
    matches.append((term, chapter, line_idx+1, line.strip()))

by_chapter = defaultdict(list)
for term, chapter, line_no, line in matches:
    by_chapter[chapter].append((term, line_no, line))

for chapter, items in by_chapter.items():
    print("=== ", chapter, " ===")
    for term, line_no, line in items:
        print(f"{line_no:4d}: [{term}] {line}")
    print()

def make_snippet(line, term):
    # highlight term in context
    idx = line.lower().find(term.lower())
    if idx == -1:
        return line.strip()
    start = max(0, idx-40)
    end = min(len(line), idx+40)
    snippet = line[start:end].strip()
    return snippet

structured = {}
for term, chapter, line_no, line in matches:
    structured.setdefault(chapter, []).append({
        "term": term,
        "line_no": line_no,
        "snippet": make_snippet(line, term)
    })

# Show a sample for a chapter
structured["Chapter 4: Glass, Hands — (Jhace POV)"]

[ASSISTANT]
dedup_structured = {}
for chapter, items in structured.items():
    seen = set()
    out = []
    for it in items:
        key = (it["line_no"], it["term"].lower())
        if key in seen:
            continue
        seen.add(key)
        out.append(it)
    dedup_structured[chapter] = out

# Quick check counts
for chap in sorted(dedup_structured.keys()):
    print(chap, "->", len(dedup_structured[chap]))

[ASSISTANT]
# Map lowercase term root to category
category_map = {}
for cat, words in banned.items():
    for w in words:
        category_map[w.lower()] = cat

for chapter, items in dedup_structured.items():
    for it in items:
        root = it["term"].lower().rstrip('s')
        # map 'hours'->'hour', 'days'->'day', etc
        if root not in category_map and root.endswith('e'): # handle 'minutes' etc
            root = root.rstrip('e')
        cat = category_map.get(root, category_map.get(it["term"].lower(), ""))
        it["category"] = cat

dedup_structured["Chapter 4: Glass, Hands — (Jhace POV)"]

report_lines = []
for chap in sorted(dedup_structured.keys(), key=lambda x: int(re.search(r"Chapter\s+(\d+)", x).group(1))):
    report_lines.append(f"## {chap}")
    for it in sorted(dedup_structured[chap], key=lambda d: d["line_no"]):
        term = it["term"]
        cat = it["category"]
        ln = it["line_no"]
        snip = it["snippet"]
        report_lines.append(f"- Line {ln}: `{term}` ({cat}) — …{snip}…")
    report_lines.append("")

print("\n".join(report_lines[:1200]))

[ASSISTANT]
hard = {}
soft = {}
for chap, items in dedup_structured.items():
    for it in items:
        term_l = it["term"].lower()
        cat = it["category"]
        # classify
        if cat == "time":
            if term_l in ["seconds","hours","hour","day","days","week","weeks","year","years","minute","minutes","sec","min","hr"]:
                hard.setdefault(chap, []).append(it)
            elif term_l.startswith("second"):  # ordinal uses
                soft.setdefault(chap, []).append(it)
            else:
                soft.setdefault(chap, []).append(it)
        elif cat == "distance":
            # yard/foot body/location uses; treat as soft collisions
            soft.setdefault(chap, []).append(it)
        else:
            soft.setdefault(chap, []).append(it)

print("Hard counts:")
for chap in sorted(hard.keys(), key=lambda x:int(re.search(r"Chapter\s+(\d+)",x).group(1))):
    print(chap, "->", len(hard[chap]))
print("\nSoft counts:")
for chap in sorted(soft.keys(), key=lambda x:int(re.search(r"Chapter\s+(\d+)",x).group(1))):
    print(chap, "->", len(soft[chap]))

Good, this is concrete. We’re not touching a single comma; just flagging where the prose breaks your measurement lexicon.

Big picture:

- You’re **mostly** compliant with the Te’Oga time/measure system.
- The only real leaks are:
  - Earth **time units**: `seconds`, `hours`, `day`, `week`, `years`.
  - A bunch of `second` as **ordinals** (second frame, second clamp, etc.) — these are *probably* fine, but I’ll mark them as “soft collisions.”
  - `yard` as a **place** (the yard / yard gate) — not a unit, but it collides textually with the banned distance word.
  - `foot` used as a body part (not a distance unit) — lexicon table bans `foot` as *distance*, not as anatomy.

I’ll give you two lists:

- **HARD CONFLICTS** – must-fix to obey the measurement lex.
- **SOFT COLLISIONS** – optional clean-up if you want zero Earthy echoes.

Line numbers are from `gthN01.md`, but the snippets will make them easy to spot in your editor.

## TL;DR / What you actually need to do

**Must-fix to be lex-compliant:**

- Replace all uses of **`hours`, `seconds`, `day`, `week`, `years`, `hour`** listed in the HARD section with the appropriate Te’Oga time units:
  - Short spans → **breaths, strokes, sets, spells, watches**  
  - Daily-scale → **tides, anneals**  
  - Longer spans → **Crucibles, Castings** (or equivalents from your broader canon)

**Optional but worth considering:**

- Decide if you care about:
  - `second` as an ordinal (11 occurrences).
  - `yard` as a location name.
  - `foot` as anatomy.

Right now, the only **true** measurement-system violations are those 14 time-unit lines. Fix those, and this novella snaps pretty cleanly into the lexicon you’ve defined. The rest is how obsessive you feel like being about Earth noise in the language.

# THE GRIP THAT HOLDS

## Chapter 1: Something Wrong — (Jhace POV)

Kindling light seeped down the Underface in a thin wash, barely enough to make the chalk marks shine. Jhace tasted limestone dust and old heat. The grid hummed under his boots—good tone, steady, a watch's worth since the last check. He ran his thumb along a riser seam anyway, feeling for the small betrayals: a grit line, a warmth that wasn't earned, a whisper where there should be a throat-sung note.

"Torque key," he said.

Chloen already had it out, two spans of oiled steel, teeth still sharp. She moved like a tally of nerves wrapped in a hand of resolve. Bram stood back with the posture of a man pretending to be at rest, copper bracer scuffed to the bone under its patina. He pretended a lot. Never about the work.

"Saddle pin's shy a quarter-turn," Jhace said. "Hear it?"

Chloen cocked her head. "I hear hum."

"Hum's not the song," Bram said. "What's the song, girl?"

Chloen squinted, tongue pinned against a molar as if that might wring sound from steel. The grid breathed through the riser—soft, regular, three heads of pressure on the gauge window, fogged at the edges. A good note rose in the forearm of pipe that crossed the catwalk, then sagged just a finger as it ran into the vertical. Tiny, like the difference between a hand laid for comfort and a hand put there to hold.

"Not square?" she guessed.

"Square is angle," Jhace said, taking the key. "This is appetite." He set the teeth, pulled until the pin bit and seated, then let his weight hang for a breath. Metal talked through his palm—grit eased, chatter smoothed, song tightened to scribe-true. He marked a small X with chalk, then a circle around it—done and checked. "There."

Chloen's breath steamed in the cool of the Underface. "Wish the grid would say words."

"It does," Bram said. "Jhace just listens hard enough to make the rest of us look deaf."

"Bram," Jhace warned, but gently. Praise felt like someone pressing their hand to his back. Good until you remembered how easy a push could be.

They moved. Catwalk over the sump run, up a ladder with rungs a hand narrow of finger-true, across a beam that had seen better tides. The Underface carried the city's heat the way bone bears weight: mostly without complaint. They'd been walking since Pouring, three watches of steady checks—clamps, joints, hangers. Chalk on the good, red hash on the suspect. Ask for a fix order and Bram would reel one off without looking at the list. Ask Jhace and he'd tell you which joints were already thinking about failing.

They reached Junction 2-nine, a cross where four risers converged into a spine and hauled warmth uptown. The hum here was brighter. And under it—there it was—a sourness. Jhace's forearms prickled.

"Something's off," he said.

Bram sniffed the air like he could catch it. "You always say that before you say what it is."

Jhace crouched by the leftmost riser, pressed his ear to the metal. The world narrowed to skin and tone. Hiss. A vein of grit. A lick of heat where heat didn't belong. He slid the key over the saddle pin and tested. It moved too free. He could move it with a breath. "Who last touched this?" he asked.

"Yesterday," Chloen said, checking the marks. "Circle and X. Your hand."

He checked the chalk and saw his own scrawl. He knew how the mark felt—chalk powder slicking the ridge of his forefinger, the jerk of his wrist when he closed the circle. He didn't remember leaving it too loose. He wouldn't. Metal didn't lie. Memory did. "Like the collapse that took them," the thought pressed, untidy as fallen brick. He swallowed and filed it: not for now.

"Grid's changing," Bram said, as if reading the thought he hadn't voiced. "Since Shapetide, the whole city's got a different tilt. Feels like a bar laid a finger thin of level."

Jhace tightened the saddle a quarter-turn, then another, until the sour note bled into the good. It should have settled him. It didn't. A copper taste crept up the back of his throat. He swallowed and got chalk for his trouble.

"You're chewing the air," Bram said. "Stop it. Air doesn't care about being chewed."

He set the key down. "Next."

They crossed to the far riser. Chloen leaned in where she shouldn't have and nearly put her sleeve to a friction burn.

"Gloves," Jhace said, already catching her wrist and moving her back a span. The admonition came automatic, tempered to not shame. "If you want to keep skin."

"Skin grows back," she said, trying for a joke and missing it.

"Not the same," Bram murmured.

Jhace didn't look up. He listened again, and this time the hum threw a stutter through his skull that made his teeth hurt. It was a half-breath delay, a not-quite-synced echo. He pressed his palm along the joint and felt the split—no, not a split; a laziness in the fit. Good enough for eye-true. Not for pressure. He chalked a red hash, then a grind mark—fix order. Bram's long arm reached over his shoulder and added a second grind mark. Priority moved up the list.

Chloen watched the marks go down like they were a script she could learn to read if she stared hard enough. "You two make it look easy."

"It isn't," Bram said. "That's why we do it."

"You mean that backwards," Chloen said, grinning, and Bram ruffled her hair, which she suffered like a cat forced to enjoy affection.

They paced the catwalk. The Underface opened in a long ribbed hall, risers touching the spine at regular bars. The world above was work and shouting; down here was breath and song. A small beauty. Jhace gathered those where he could. The world had taken a lot and was greedy still; he let himself have a handful of small things when it wasn't looking. The heat against his palm. Chalk dust on skin. The way Chloen's questions came faster when she forgot to be ashamed of not knowing.

Bram fell into step beside him, boots hitting metal at the same cadence. "You working alone again tonight?"

"We've got Junction seven to recheck," Jhace said.

"That's not what I asked."

Jhace gave him silence; it was easier than lying, and it made Bram do the talking he always wanted to do anyway.

"You're good with metal," Bram said, gentling the words so they didn't bite. "Less good with people."

Jhace scrubbed chalk off his thumb. "Metal doesn't leave."

The quiet that followed had a weight to it, like a clamp you'd tightened too far. Bram fit words into it carefully. "Your parents didn't leave you. They died."

"That's a kind of leaving," Jhace said, and the bitterness tasted like grit. He didn't want Chloen hearing this, didn't want his wound made into a training story. He pointed at the next riser to move them along. "Check the hanger bolts. Two spans apart, finger-true."

Chloen went quick, grateful to be useful. Bram gave Jhace a look that said the talk wasn't done, then let it be, because he was not a fool and the work took priority. Always the work.

They got three more risers in before the song went wrong enough that even Chloen heard it. The hum lifted half a pitch and held there like a breath someone forgot to release. Jhace's arm hair rose. The copper taste sharpened until it felt like a coin under his tongue.

"What—" Chloen began.

"Stop," Jhace said. Every word came out flat and square. He took the key back from her hand and set it down. "Don't touch anything."

Bram moved behind him and took a long slow breath—one, two, three, four, five—like he was counting how long it took panic to set. "Pressure's climbing. Gauges say three heads and a half. Shouldn't be."

"Where's it feeding from?" Jhace asked.

"Upstream," Bram said. "Or skyward, if you like your nightmares literal."

The light changed. Not brighter—thicker. As if someone had dipped the whole Underface in glass that hadn't cooled yet. Shadows deepened by a hair, a strange quarter-turn twist to the air, an edge where a smooth should be. Jhace tasted the moment it tipped. He'd never had a word for it. He would later. For now it was that wrongness you feel when a beam you trusted shifts underfoot.

"Back," Jhace said. "Two strides. Hands on rail."

Chloen obeyed without thought, bless her quick-heart. Bram didn't move, because Bram was a stubborn old bastard and the grid was his and he'd never step back from it. Jhace grabbed his sleeve and pulled anyway, two spans of force, enough to make a point. Bram followed, but only because he chose to.

The hum became a tremor. Not in the risers—in the air. The Underface breathed in, walls a hand closer without moving, then held that breath too long. Jhace's eyes watered. He blinked and the world wavered like heat above a quench pool.

"What in the—" Bram began.

The tremor stacked, layer on layer, until the catwalk shivered under their boots. The whine pierced through, high and thin, threading down from above like a needle of pure frequency. It bypassed his ears, went straight to the bones of his jaw. The grid's song bent under it, a harmony twisted out of shape.

Jhace looked up. Something massive was descending from the sky.

## Chapter 2: Warped Horizon — (Tiffani POV)

Tiffani Merrow stood in the vaulted hush of the Glass Quarter observatory, her angle-cage a brass scaffold of plumb-weights and sighting frames. The air carried the faint tang of polished lens and spirit level, a scent that grounded her when the world outside refused to. She pressed her eye to the main eyepiece, the micrometer dial clicking under her thumb like a heartbeat she could count.

The horizon waited, unyielding. Three spans from the Crown Spire baseline, the deflection read one point one eight fingers inward—systematic, repeatable, impossible. She logged it in the ledger, her script hair-true despite the stiffness creeping into her knuckles. Numbers didn't bend. They demanded you bend to them.

Mikel hovered at the secondary frame, his notations a breath behind. "Stable on parallax," he said, voice tentative as unannealed glass.

"Parallax is constant," Tiffani replied, not lifting her gaze. "We're measuring deviation from true. East baseline, repeat the vernier."

He flushed, adjusted the scale. "One point one eight fingers. Same as last set."

She nodded once, cross-referencing against the prior log. The bow had deepened since Shapetide—a finger's breadth in three watches, curving the line like a riser under uneven load. No instrument flaw; she'd calibrated the cage twice at dawn. This was the world tilting, geometry whispering of a failure deeper than any span collapse.

"Why alone?" Mikel asked, the question slipping out like a chip in a mold. He was young, still chasing the warmth of shared work over solitary precision.

"Precision requires isolation," she said, her tone level as the bubble in her gauge. "Variables multiply with company. People... deviate."

He marked the log anyway, the scratch of his chalk a small concession to silence. Tiffani felt the weight of it, the unspoken: her fortress of focus, built after Marisse's fall. Her mentor had trusted a rushed span, politicians' optimism over three unchecked measurements. The collapse had taken her in a cascade of proof-glass and iron. Tiffani had measured the debris afterward—every fractured angle, every deviated line. Numbers didn't leave. They stayed, cold and certain, to teach you.

She shifted to the Crown Spire sightline, running the trigonometry in her head. The deflection held, a systematic curve that mocked the flat true of established geodesics. The eastern horizon cupped inward, as if the expanse beyond were drawing breath. She logged the fourth reading, then a fifth for tolerance. The data piled like unstruck blows.

Mikel tried again, softer. "The festival tonight—glass-blowers from the lower grids. Demonstration pour. You could... observe."

"Collating," Tiffani said, already turning the dial for a western baseline. The observatory's proof-walls hummed faintly, carrying the city's distant pulse. She preferred this rhythm: measurable, predictable. People brought echoes she couldn't scribe.

The boy sighed, a small pressure drop in the room's air. She noted it, filed it under costs. Clarity had edges. They cut.

The sixth measurement locked in. Horizon impossible. The bow deepened another hair-width, the line no longer straight but strained, like a cable under lift-heavy tension. Tiffani straightened, her spine aligning to plumb. Then the roar began—a low bellow rising from the stone, as if the world itself had decided to answer.

## Chapter 3: The Piercing — (Jhace POV)

The whine sharpened, threading through the grid's hum like a fault line in a brace. Jhace's jaw buzzed, fillings aching as if gnawed by unseen teeth. The Underface held its breath, walls inching closer in the thickened light, shadows pooling deeper than they should. Gauges trembled at three heads and climbing, needles quivering like compass arms in a storm.

"Up," Jhace said, voice flat against the rising pitch. "Lift. Now."

Chloen moved first, scrambling for the access gate. Bram lingered a breath, eyes on the risers as if willing them to confess. The tremor rolled through the catwalk, a shiver in the air that raised dust from seams long sealed. Jhace grabbed Chloen's arm, propelled her toward the shaft. Bram followed without argument—rare enough to note, but the grid's song had soured to a growl.

The lift cage rattled as they piled in, chains groaning under unearned weight. Jhace slapped the release, the mechanism grinding upward in fits, the whine from above now a bellow that vibrated his sternum. Pressure stacked, layer on layer, the air turning viscous, pressing inward like a clamp overtightened on soft iron. His ears popped, once, twice, the world muffling to a distant roar.

Halfway up, the impact hit.

It wasn't sound first. It was the world inhaling. A bone-deep compression, as if Te'Oga had drawn a breath too vast for its ribs. The lift lurched sideways—not down, but athwart, gravity twisting like a hanger pin sheared under torque. Jhace's stomach flipped, bile rising with the copper tang that coated his tongue. The cage swung, chains singing a high discord, and for three breaths, up became irrelevant. Everything fell wrong: tools from his belt scattering in lazy arcs, Chloen's chalk clattering against the far wall as if flung by an idle hand.

Then light tore.

Through the cage's grate, Jhace glimpsed it—a white-hot line slashing the sky above, impossibly straight, punching down from zenith to horizon. Not a streak, but a cut: clouds convulsing like flesh from a blade, atmosphere buckling in rippling waves that bent the air into heat-haze shimmers. The line widened as it descended, a world-vent projectile vast as a grid-span, its edges glowing lemon-bright, trailing a wake of distorted sky. Light itself warped in its passage, casting the city in fractured glints—shadows quarter-turned, edges where smooth planes should be.

The bellow arrived late, a delayed roar that slammed into them like a pour of slag. It rattled the cage, shook loose rivets from the shaft walls, sent them pattering down like hot rain. The Underface answered below: a chorus of metal screaming in torsion, risers venting steam in white plumes that scalded the dark. Gauges would be spinning wild now, pressure bursting seams, but Jhace couldn't hear over the grind—the proof-walls above cracking like overquenched glass, their spiderweb fractures propagating in visible lines.

The lift jolted to a halt, midway, the mechanism seized. "Out," Jhace barked, shouldering the gate. It stuck, metal warped a finger off true. He rammed it with his hip, the frame giving just enough. They spilled onto the access ledge, the world tilting underfoot—not the familiar cant of worn stone, but a planetary lurch, the ground heaving as if shoved from below. Gravity misbehaved in fits: Chloen's boot skidded sideways, pulling her toward a rail that hadn't been there a breath ago; Bram staggered, one hand slapping a bulkhead that groaned in reply.

"Stay low," Jhace said, dropping to hands and knees. The air thrummed with secondary shocks—pipes bursting in the depths, their hisses turning to shrieks as superheated vapor jetted free. Dust rained, thick as a veil, coating his tongue with grit and the acrid bite of scorched insulation. The roar rolled on, horizon bulging outward in his blurred vision, lines that once held plumb now sagging like a beam under unbraced load.

They crawled the ledge, spans of twisted catwalk ahead, braces buckling with pops like struck anvils. Jhace led, one hand testing each rung, the other hauling Chloen when her grip slipped. Bram brought up the rear, his bracer scraping stone as he muttered curses at the failing world. A secondary wave hit midway—pressure dropping sudden, sucking air from lungs, then slamming back with force enough to bruise ribs. The access shaft vented below, a geyser of steam and debris blasting upward, singeing Jhace's sleeve to threads.

They reached the surface hatch as the first proof-wall gave. It was the eastern one, a monolith of layered stone and iron a rod thick, designed to hold against vein-mass quakes. It shattered with a crack like worlds parting—glittering shards spreading in drifts, the wall folding inward along stress paths Jhace could trace in his mind: unchecked seams from last anneal, a hair off square in the foundational pour. Debris avalanched, swallowing a market stall whole, the screams rising thin and sharp over the din.

Jhace kicked the hatch free, daylight spilling in fractured— the sky a wound, the white line's scar fading to orange glow at its edges, atmosphere still rippling like water struck by a dropped ingot. They tumbled out into chaos: streets canted a stride off level, buildings leaning into one another like drunks at anneal's end, hangers snapping with reports that echoed the initial roar. Steam pipes burst in the midribs, veiling districts in scalding fog; risers vented plasma arcs that lit the dust-choked air lemon-bright.

"Chloen—stay with Bram," Jhace said, hauling himself up. His ears rang, a constant drone that muffled the triage shouts, the grind of settling rubble. Nausea roiled, gravity's sideways pull lingering in his gut, but he pushed it down. This was collapse. This was big. The kind that took parents if you let it. He wouldn't run from another.

He moved toward the heart of the wrongness, boots skidding on glass-slick stone—shards from shattered proof-windows, edges hair-sharp. The ground trembled in aftershocks, cracks propagating like chalk hashes gone feral, swallowing a handcart whole. People staggered from the haze: a vendor clutching a scalded arm, his face twisted in silent scream; a brace of workers hauling a pinned man from a collapsed awning, their grunts lost in the din. Jhace veered toward a fallen rib—a heat-spine toppled across a glass-house forecourt, its weight crushing the proof-wall inward, molten gather pooling beneath in cherry-glow pools.

There, amid the wreckage: pale hands straining against a buckled beam, fingers splayed in precise defiance. A woman—dark hair matted with dust, face pale but set—pinned at the leg under the rib's overhang, a spill of molten glass searing her calf where it had splashed free. The beam pinned her thigh a hand above the knee, iron groaning as she wedged a shard of proof-glass beneath for leverage. No scream, just gritted teeth and a glare that said she measured her own ruin and found it unacceptable.

Jhace didn't think. He dropped beside her, gloved hands testing the beam's edge. "Hold still. I'll pry."

Her eyes flicked to him—blue-sharp, assessing. "Leverage point's three fingers in. Torque from the low end."

He nodded, no time for questions. The beam massed half a stone easy, its load path fouled by the collapse. Nearby, a burly glass-puller staggered from the haze, pry bar in hand—his face soot-streaked, but steady. "On three," Jhace said, stripping his right glove. The metal radiated blood-heat, but the glass spill was worse: cherry-bright at the edges, cooling to dull red where it kissed her skin. Blisters rose already, flesh bubbling with a sizzle that turned his stomach.

"One," the puller grunted, wedging the bar.

"Two." Jhace's bare palm met the spill's edge—agony lanced, heat leaping like a live wire into his veins. But it didn't stop there. The warmth rerouted, pulling inward, as if his skin were a quench bath drawing fire from the pour. The glass cooled under his touch, cracking with a brittle snap, shards flaking away to reveal cooled slag. His hand charred, skin blistering black, but the searing pull eased on her leg— the molten edge dulling to hand-warm, then chill.

"Three!" The beam shifted, inching up on their heave. She yanked free, leg trailing blood and glass flecks, but whole. The puller dropped the bar, staggering back as another tremor rolled through. "You—your hand—"

Jhace waved him off, the copper taste flooding his mouth now, thick as molten. A line of heat traced his forearm—not burn, but wire-drawn, glowing faint copper-gold under skin. Vein-burn, though he had no name for it yet. The world spun, nausea cresting.

She rose on her good leg, steadying against the beam. "You pulled the heat. How?"

Before he could answer, a cry cut through—Chloen's voice, thin and broken. "Jhace!"

He turned, the puller forgotten. Twenty spans off, amid a drift of shattered proof-wall, Bram knelt over a crumpled form. Chloen lay twisted, head wound gaping from a flung shard, blood sheeting her face. Her breaths came shallow, ragged, chest hitching without rhythm. Skull fracture, Jhace knew in the gut-sick way he knew failing joints—pressure building inside, no outlet.

He ran, knees buckling on the canted stone, the sideways gravity pulling like a bad weld. Bram looked up, face ashen. "Shard caught her. She's—"

Jhace dropped beside her, hands going to the wound automatic. Blood welled hot between his fingers, pulse fluttering weak under his thumb. "Chloen. Eyes on me." No response, just the faint rattle in her throat. The world narrowed: the roar fading to a hum, the dust settling in her hair like chalk dust from a good day's mark. She was his tally of nerves wrapped in resolve, the one he'd sworn not to lose like the others. Not to a collapse he couldn't feel coming.

Heat bloomed in his palm again, unbidden—the copper-gold line flaring brighter, warmth flooding down his arm like poured metal seeking mold. It spilled into her, not fire but mend: a rerouting of fracture lines, bone knitting under skin with a faint crackle like cooling slag. The gash closed, edges sealing seamless, color returning to her cheeks in a slow tide. Her breath evened, eyes fluttering open—confused, but clear.

"Jhace?" she whispered, voice small.

He pulled back, the glow fading, exhaustion crashing like a dropped load. His vision tunneled, the vein-line throbbing at a finger's width now, permanent as a scribe mark. Vomit rose, sour and inevitable; he turned aside, retching chalk and bile onto the dust.

The woman—pale, precise—limped up, eyes wide on his hands. The burn scar smoked faintly on his palm, raw and weeping, but the glow's echo lingered in his veins. "Can you walk?" he rasped, wiping his mouth.

She tested her leg, wincing but steady. "Yes." A pause, her gaze tracing the copper trace up his arm. "What did you just do?"

Jhace met her eyes, the world still ringing, the sky's scar bleeding orange above. "I don't know."

She stared at his hands, the glow's afterimage fading to nothing. The world had changed. And so had he.

## Chapter 4: Breath Catch — (Jhace POV)

Cooltide wrapped Bram's forge in a hush broken only by the coals' low sigh, their banked heat casting long shadows across the anvil and tool racks. Jhace perched on the edge of the stool, his bandaged right hand throbbing in time with the vein-line's faint itch—a copper ridge three fingers long now, etched under skin like a fault waiting to propagate. Three tides since the Piercing, and the world still carried the scar: streets canted a stride off true, the grid's hum laced with that persistent third-note whine, as if the whole expanse had drawn a breath it couldn't release.

Bram worked the herbal salve into a clean linen wrap, his bracer—scuffed patina gleaming in the ember light—brushing Jhace's forearm as he rebound the palm. "Burn's deep, but clean. No rot. And that glow you pulled... copper-gold, like the heart of a pour. Felt it reroute the heat, didn't it? Like bleeding a riser gone wild."

Jhace flexed his fingers, the scar pulling tight, a map of borrowed fire. "Felt it everywhere. Pulled the glass off her leg, then... Chloen. Sealed her like mending a split seam. But the cost—" He glanced to the alcove where Chloen slept, her breaths even now, head wound scribed to nothing but a faint bruise. "Emptied me. Like I'd hung my whole weight on a single hanger."

Bram tied off the wrap, his grip steady but gentle, the kind that said he'd lost apprentices before and wouldn't lose this one to silence. "The cut cracked more than proof-walls. Grid's off-key, horizons bowed like you'd measured. You think it's just you feeling it deeper?"

Jhace met his eyes, the forge's warmth a small brace against the chill seeping from the vein. "Feels like I traded skin for something I can't torque back. Metal speaks plain. This... whispers."

Bram grunted, wiping salve from his hands on a rag. "Whispers or roars, the work's the same. Listen, mend, mark it done. Your parents—" He paused, fitting the words careful as a saddle pin. "They'd say the same. Hold what you can, when you can. Rest now. Junction seven waits, but not at the cost of your grip."

The door creaked open, admitting a figure on a makeshift crutch of lashed iron and proof-shard—pale skin dusted with travel grit, dark hair bound back in a guild-practical knot. She scanned the space like a vernier sweep: tools aligned, coals banked, air thick with salve and coal-smoke. Her leg favored the splint, bound clean but scarred at the calf where molten glass had kissed. "Jhace Torrins," she said, not as question but datum, her voice level as a bubble gauge. "I measured the route from the Glass Quarter. Two reaches east, accounting for the new cant. Tiffani Merrow."

Bram straightened, bracer scraping the workbench. "Glass-guild surveyor. Word's out you clocked the bow before the line fell. Data that held true."

She nodded once, crutch tapping stone as she limped closer, her free hand flexing—knuckles unmarked yet, but the motion held a precision that spoke of tolerances already tested. Her eyes fixed on Jhace's bandage, then flicked to the alcove, Chloen's sleeping form. "The thermal pull on the beam. Bare skin to cherry-glass, no quench. And the girl—skull fracture knit seamless under your hands. Copper-gold resonance, contained but directed. I've cross-referenced echoes in the old ledgers—affinity flares, post-cataclysm. But not like that. Not instinctive."

Jhace shifted on the stool, the anvil's edge digging cold into his thigh. "Not chasing guild theories. Grid's venting wild up top; junctions need checks, not scrolls."

Tiffani's jaw tightened a fraction, a line drawn taut against deviation. She eased the crutch aside, drawing a slate from her satchel—chalked vectors already, simple force lines converging on a fracture node, rerouted through a central brace. "Theories brace failures. You forced connection without measure—mended flesh and flow on pull alone. It's affinity, Wholeness-touched. But raw, it burns unchecked." She set the slate between them, her finger tracing the node. "Instinct listens; form guides. Let me demonstrate."

He eyed the diagram, lines clean as hair-true scribe-work, angles holding plumb where his gut-feel blurred. Metal didn't need vectors; it needed ear and palm. But the vein itched, a reminder of power loosed without clamp or key. "One test," he said, pushing up from the stool. "Scrap brace. If it seats, we log it."

She nodded, limping to the scrap pile by the quench trough—selected a fouled hanger, twisted a quarter-turn from the Piercing's torque, stress chattering faint under eye. "Palm here. Feel the deviation—the appetite pulling off-axis."

Jhace stripped the fresh bandage, scar raw but steady, and pressed to the iron. The warp hummed wrong, a sour echo of the grid's third note, vectors invisible but felt in the lazy drag. "Pulls east under load. Half-turn shy."

"Now redirect." Her hand guided his—cool, measured, no tremor yet—tracing the chalked path. "Not brute torque. Bleed the stress like overpressure in a vein. Let the warmth circuit the node."

He leaned in, the copper line flaring faint under skin. Warmth stirred, not wild but channeled—gold threading the metal like poured mend seeking mold. The hanger straightened with a soft chime, settling true to eye, no chatter under thumb-test. Seam held, load path aligned.

Tiffani exhaled, satisfaction in the set of her shoulders. "Your resonance seeks wholeness—connections rewoven. Mine overlays form: geometry to hold the mend. Without it, affinity frays." She flexed her own hand again, a subtle stiffness threading the joints, blue-silver faint at the edges like developing patina. "The cut gifted sight—stress lines visible, tolerances scribed in air. We could balance. Your ear to my angles."

Bram watched from the coals, a low rumble of approval. "Sharp as a torque tooth. Might keep the burn from going wild."

Jhace rebound his palm, the linen settling like a temporary clamp. The vein quieted, not erased but braced. "Tomorrow. Junction seven recheck. If your vectors hold there..."

"Logged." She gathered the slate and crutch, tapping toward the door. At the threshold, she paused, horizon's bow implicit in her stance. "The world deviates. We measure the brace—or it measures us."

The door shut, forge falling to coal-whisper. Jhace traced the scar through linen, heat's memory a weight he could carry. Bram clapped his shoulder, bracer solid. "She's got lines you don't. Might teach you to see the tilt coming."

Jhace nodded, the grid's distant hum filtering through stone—off-key, but not failed. "Might." Rest called, but the work waited. Always.

## Interlude 1: Facets of Fracture

### Corlexi — Form

Corlexi gripped the midrib span's proof-brace, her fingers splayed against the stone's subtle cant, the Piercing's torque etched as a hairline deviation in the load path. Dust still sifted from cracks above, the air thick with the acrid bite of burst steam and scorched patina, but her new sight cut through: blue-silver lattices overlaying every surface, stress vectors arcing like flawed pours, demanding alignment. The eastern brace pulled a quarter-turn off plumb, a cascade threat propagating unseen.

She pressed harder, affinity answering—a geometric compulsion, Form's unyielding call to integrity. The lattice brightened under her touch, lines snapping taut with a chime like crystal struck true. Vectors realigned, stone groaning as it settled into perfect angle, the brace locking flawless against the tilt. The span held, a bastion of precision amid the settling ruin, every joint hair-true.

But her knuckles locked, joints calcifying with blue-silver flecks that spread like cooling slag, mobility shedding in increments she could measure but not halt. She flexed them once, ignoring the cost—the faint tremor in her grip, the way the world blurred at the edges unless viewed through angles. Deviation was fracture; she would force every line straight, every structure to recall its mold. The cut had bent the expanse; she would re-form it, even if her hands forgot how to yield.

### Mobel — Purity

Mobel knelt in the lower grid's sump, steam hissing from a vented riser like impure breath, his palms pressed to the scalded arm of a pinned scavenger. The man's flesh bubbled with inhaled vapor, corruption threading vein by vein—fouled, unchecked, a stain leaching into the clean flow. The Piercing's bellow still thrummed in Mobel's skull, but it had kindled something sharper: a white-fire urge to divide, to excise what the wound had tainted.

He channeled it, hands flaring stark white, not mending but separating—the impurity drawn into himself like dross skimmed from molten, burned clean in a flare that left only wholeness behind. The man's arm cooled, skin sealing unmarked, breaths coming sharp and unclouded. Mobel rose, the scavenger's gasp of thanks lost in the haze, but his own veins itched with the residue, a creeping burn that blurred mercy into zeal.

The world leaked chaos now, the projectile's scar weeping grit and fracture into every seam. Mobel would purge it—flesh from taint, stone from flaw, doubt from will. Purity required the cut: clean from corrupt, whole from waste. His hands steadied, not in fatigue, but resolve. The fire would refine. It must.




## Chapter 5: First Hold — (Tiffani POV)

The Underface's ribbed gloom stretched ahead like a flawed mold, risers converging into the spine at Junction seven with seams etched raw by the Piercing's torque—a quarter-turn deviation in every joint, pressure gauges fogged at two heads and climbing slow but systematic. Tiffani leaned into her crutch, the wood-and-iron brace biting her palm as she balanced the slate on her knee, chalk tracing vectors across the haze of suspended dust. Stress lines glowed blue-silver in her sight, load paths fraying where the world's cant pulled uneven, tolerances exceeded by a hair-width per tide. Four tides since the cut, and her leg bore the scar's persistent itch—functional at ninety percent, the burn's edge a constant reminder of molten glass cooled under Jhace's impossible pull. But the new perception compensated: lattices scribed in air where once she'd relied on angle-cage and vernier, deviations now visible as glowing fractures, begging realignment.

Jhace crouched at the leftmost riser, torque key in his good hand as he tested a saddle pin, his bandaged palm hovering deliberate despite the vein-line's faint throb—three fingers of copper ridge visible when his sleeve rode up, a mark she'd logged in her ledger as baseline cost. Chloen shadowed him close, her chalk marks surer since the healing that had knit her skull seamless, no longer the tentative apprentice but a quick-study with questions that cut like scribe-true edges. Bram oversaw from the catwalk above, his bracer gleaming dull under the kindling wash seeping from vents, his posture a steady brace against the grid's off-key hum. Tiffani observed their rhythm: Jhace's instinct probing seams where her angles predicted failure, his warmth seeking the flaws she'd mapped with unerring precision. It tugged at her internal variables, this offset synchronization—efficiency potential blooming like a well-calculated pour, but laced with an uncontrolled factor: the way his presence deviated her focus, pulling it from pure data toward something warmer, less quantifiable.

"Node here," she said, tapping the slate's central cross with her chalk, the motion sending a faint drag through her knuckles—baseline stiffness, barely noticeable yet, but logged as a creeping cost. "East vector deviates half a finger under projected load. Brace it low, or the chatter builds exponential, risking vent at three heads."

Jhace pressed his ear to the metal, the world narrowing for him to tone and vibration, his breath steaming faint in the cool. "Appetite's pulling already. Feels the laziness in the fit." He set the key's teeth, twisted until the pin bit and seated with a resonant click—the hum steadying from erratic stutter to a clean, throat-sung note that echoed up the riser. "Your lines call it square. No drag left."

She nodded once, limping a span closer, the crutch's tap echoing her pulse against the stone, a measured rhythm that grounded her amid the grid's persistent third-note whine. The stiffness in her knuckles held steady at baseline—a faint drag on the chalk as she updated the vector—but the lattice in her sight sharpened with each invocation, blue-silver threading deeper into her perception, turning every glance into a geodesic map. "Now test the resonance. Redirect through the node—let the warmth follow the path I've scribed. Not force, but guidance."

He stripped the bandage partial, the scar on his palm raw but unyielding, a charred map of heat rerouted in the Piercing's chaos. His hand met the joint, and the glow flickered to life—copper-gold at first faint, then blooming as his affinity answered her call, warmth rerouting the warp along the invisible lines she'd drawn. In her sight, the vectors straightened with a soft chime, like proof-glass settling true in a quench frame, the deviation bleeding away until the riser exhaled steady, pressure easing back to a stable two heads with no lingering grit-vein to threaten burst.

Chloen let out a low whistle from her perch on the catwalk ladder, her eyes wide on the seamless seam where warp had been. "Like the cut never torqued it at all. Clean pour from end to end—no hash needed."

Bram grunted approval from above, his long arm reaching down to test the pin himself, fingers probing the seat with a thumb-press that spoke decades of grid-work. "Holds solid under load. First true song in this junction since the line fell. Solid brace, girl—your vectors and his pull make a clamp worth marking."

Tiffani logged the correction in her ledger, her script flowing steady despite the subtle ache now threading her fingers—the cost of channeling sight, a hair more calcification per invocation, joints beginning to resist the flex. The hold hummed between them all: Jhace's instinctive pull bleeding the deviation clean, her geometric map guiding it home without waste. Partnership, not yet named but undeniably functional—load paths shared across affinities, tolerances extended beyond what either could achieve isolated. It deviated her internal equations, this synergy, pulling her from solitary precision toward a shared vector, but the data supported it: efficiency up by a measurable margin, failures preempted before they chattered.

They shifted seamless to the cross-riser, Jhace's thumb already tracing a suspect hanger she'd flagged in her initial sweep, her chalk updating the vector as he tested the seam with a palm-press. "Feels lazy in the fit," he said, his voice threading the hum like a familiar note, and she nodded immediate— "Eighth-turn deviation. Torque it north to compensate the cant."

The key turned under his grip, warmth flaring brief but guided now, the hanger seating with a click that echoed satisfaction up the catwalk. Chloen called the gauge reading a breath ahead: "Stable across the board. Two heads even, no climb." Bram reached over to add a second grind mark beside the first—priority cleared, fix order downgraded to routine.

Tiffani paused at the junction's spine, her sight sweeping the converged risers one final pass, lattices dimming as no new deviations glowed urgent. She called the halt, slate closing with a definitive snap that cut the hum. "Pressure's leveled across all nodes. Mark the junction done—no suspect lines remain, tolerances within baseline."

Jhace straightened from his crouch, wiping chalk dust from his good palm with a rag, the vein-line's copper glow faded but ever-present under his sleeve. "Felt it seat true for the first time. Song didn't drag like before—the third note wove in without souring."

Their gazes held for a measured breath—her blue-sharp assessment meeting his copper-warm resolve, the lattice in her sight dimming gradual as the echo of his warmth lingered in the air, a faint heat that deviated the cool calculus of the Underface. Respect braced the space between them, a tentative hold against the world's persistent tilt, not trust fully yet but a functional alliance that promised more. The grid hummed softer around them, the third-note dissonance woven into harmony rather than dominant discord. They turned as one toward the ladder up, her crutch-tap and his bootfall syncing in the climb—world still broken above, horizons bowed and streets canted, but this junction mended solid. For now, it was enough to log as progress.

## Chapter 6: Rhythm Set — (Jhace POV)

The Underface corridors pressed in tighter five tides after the Piercing, faint cracks spidering up the ribs like warnings left unhashed, the grid's hum laced with that unrelenting third-note dissonance—a persistent drag, as if the entire vein-system carried the memory of the cut's torque in every pulse. Jhace walked them now with Tiffani at his side, her crutch-tap falling into sync with his bootfall in a cadence that had settled without fanfare: her measured steps bracing his instinctive stride, angles offsetting the appetites he felt in the metal. The air down here tasted heavier, limestone dust mingling with the faint acrid bite of vented steam from unchecked seams, shadows pooling deeper where the kindling wash seeped thin through vents.

"Next hanger, two bars ahead," she said without needing to consult the slate tucked under her arm, her voice threading through the hum like a plumb line dropped true into murky depths. "Vector pulls east—half-turn shy under three heads, chatter building if we don't seat it low."

He nodded, torque key already palmed from his belt, his good hand testing the seam before she'd finished the sentence. "Feels the laziness creeping in. Appetite's building slow but sure." The twist bit deep under his torque, warmth flaring copper under her unspoken guidance—the glow contained now, rerouting the warp along paths he sensed but she scribed visible. The song evened out, a clean note rising from the chatter like a riser bled clean of grit. "Seated true. No pull left."

"Logged," she replied, her chalk scratching faint against the slate—knuckles dragging just a touch more than the tide before, stiffness noticeable now but not yet critical, her sight holding sharp as blue lattices scribed tolerances he felt in his bones but couldn't map without her.

Chloen trailed a span behind with Bram, her gauge calls coming a breath ahead of need, her questions yielding to efficient shorthand that spoke of growth: "Pressure holding steady?" "Two and a half heads, no climb." The crew moved fluid as a well-oiled clamp—Bram wheeling supports where Jhace pointed a flaw, Tiffani's vectors preempting the warnings his ear caught faint in the hum.
